Prompt: 'What are the risks of having high blood pressure?\n' 
Generated text: '\nThe risk of heart disease is 2 to 6 times greater if you have high blood pressure, compared to people with normal blood pressure.\n\nHigh blood pressure is often referred to as the “silent killer” because it often has no symptoms. High blood pressure can damage blood vessels, heart, kidneys, and eyes. Most people who have high blood pressure don’t know that they have it.\n\nThere are no signs or symptoms of high blood pressure. Blood pressure increases when the heart pumps more blood with each heartbeat.\n\nHow is high blood pressure measured?\n\nBlood pressure is measured using a sphygmomanometer. This is a device that measures the pressure in the arteries (blood vessels) during a blood pressure measurement.\n\nThe systolic pressure is the pressure in the artery when the heart beats. The diastolic pressure is the pressure in the artery when the heart is between beats.\n\nA normal blood pressure reading is between 120/80 mm Hg and 140/90 mm Hg. This is a systolic pressure of 120 and a diastolic pressure of 80. A person with high blood pressure has systolic and diastolic pressures of 140 and 90.\n\nHow common is high blood pressure?\n\nAbout 50% of people in the United States have high blood pressure. In Canada, about 60% of adults have high blood pressure.\n\nThere are several factors that affect how likely you are to have high blood pressure. These factors include:\n\nAge. People over age 65 have a much higher risk of high blood pressure than people under age 65.\n\nRace. African-Americans have a much higher risk of high blood pressure than white people.\n\nGender. Women have a much higher risk of high blood pressure than men.\n\nFamily history. People with a family history of high blood pressure are more likely to have high blood pressure.\n\nGenetics. Many people have genes that can cause high blood pressure. These genes do not cause high blood pressure on their own, but they increase the risk of having high blood pressure.\n\nDiagnosis\n\nHigh blood pressure is often called a “silent killer” because there are often no signs or symptoms. It’s called high blood pressure because it puts extra stress on blood vessels. If high blood pressure is not treated, it can damage blood vessels, heart, kidneys, and eyes'

Prompt: 'What lifestyle changes can help prevent and lower high blood pressure?\n' 
Generated text: 'Here are some lifestyle changes you can make to help prevent high blood pressure:\n1. Eat less salt.\nPeople with high blood pressure tend to have higher blood pressure in general. Salt is a common cause of high blood pressure, so cutting back on salt can help lower your blood pressure.\nTry to cut back on processed and packaged foods that are full of sodium. Salt is a major contributor to high blood pressure, so limiting your salt intake can help you control your blood pressure.\n2. Get plenty of potassium.\nPotassium is an electrolyte that regulates the balance of water and sodium in your blood. If you don’t have enough potassium, you can have high blood pressure.\nTo get more potassium in your diet, try to eat foods that are high in potassium. Foods like bananas, avocados, and potatoes are good sources of potassium.\n3. Limit alcohol.\nEating enough potassium is important, but so is limiting alcohol intake. Alcohol can cause increased fluid retention, which can lead to swelling of the veins. This can put extra pressure on your heart.\n4. Keep an eye on your weight.\nPeople with high blood pressure tend to be overweight. Excess weight can raise blood pressure and lead to other health problems. Keep an eye on your weight by eating a diet that is high in fruits and vegetables, lean meats, and whole grains.\n5. Exercise regularly.\nRegular exercise helps you control your weight, but it also helps you manage high blood pressure. Try to get at least 30 minutes of exercise most days of the week.\nExercise can help lower your blood pressure and boost your heart health. It can also help you manage stress.\n6. Manage stress.\nStress can cause high blood pressure. It can also make it hard to manage your blood pressure. Finding ways to reduce stress in your life can help lower your blood pressure.\nOther lifestyle changes include eating a balanced diet, getting enough sleep, and limiting caffeine and smoking. Eating a diet high in fruits and vegetables can lower your cholesterol and blood pressure.\nIf you notice any changes in your body, you should see your doctor. Your doctor can help you get your blood pressure under control.'

Prompt: 'What kind of medicines can help control high blood pressure?\n' 
Generated text: '\nA:\n\nQuick Answer\n\nSome common medicines to help control high blood pressure include diuretics, blood pressure medications, ACE inhibitors and beta-blockers. Diuretics, which help to remove excess water from the body, can help to lower blood pressure by increasing urine output. Blood pressure medications can help lower blood pressure by reducing the force of blood on the blood vessels. ACE inhibitors and beta-blockers help to relax blood vessels and reduce the force of blood on the blood vessels, which also decreases blood pressure.\n\nKeep Learning\n\nACE inhibitors and beta-blockers also increase the amount of nitric oxide in the blood, which relaxes the blood vessels and helps to decrease blood pressure. Diuretics and blood pressure medications help to decrease the amount of sodium and fluid in the body, which can help to decrease blood pressure. However, there are side effects to using some diuretics and blood pressure medications, and some diuretics can have an adverse effect on kidney function.'

Prompt: 'What are some things that can increase the risk of getting high blood pressure?\n' 
Generated text: "\nA:\n\nQuick Answer\n\nThe risk of getting high blood pressure can be increased through the consumption of certain drugs, smoking and other lifestyle habits. Other factors that may increase the risk of getting high blood pressure include a family history of high blood pressure, obesity, diabetes and being physically inactive.\n\nKeep Learning\n\nHigh blood pressure affects more than half of the adult population in the United States. About one in every three people is diagnosed with high blood pressure. High blood pressure is a major cause of heart attack and stroke. About 8 million people die of heart disease each year, and high blood pressure is a major cause.\n\nCertain drugs, such as antimalarial drugs, aspirin, steroids and some antidepressants, may increase the risk of getting high blood pressure. Smoking, particularly when smoked alongside alcohol, can increase the risk of getting high blood pressure. Diet and physical inactivity may also increase the risk of getting high blood pressure.\n\nHigh blood pressure is often thought of as a silent killer. It does not cause symptoms in many cases. To test for high blood pressure, a person will have their blood pressure measured at the doctor's office. A physician can prescribe medication to lower blood pressure if it is elevated."

Prompt: 'What is bronchiolitis and who is most susceptible to it?\n' 
Generated text: "Bronchiolitis is a swelling of the airways in the lungs.\nThe condition is more common in babies and young children and can cause shortness of breath, coughing and wheezing, and is usually mild.\nBut bronchiolitis is a serious condition that can be life-threatening if it develops in someone who is very young or older.\nThere is no cure for bronchiolitis, but treatment may make it milder or stop it from getting worse.\nBronchiolitis is a swelling of the airways in the lungs. These are pictured above\nWHAT IS BRONCHIOLITIS? Bronchiolitis is a swelling of the airways in the lungs. The condition causes shortness of breath, coughing and wheezing. It's most common in babies and young children and is usually mild. But bronchiolitis can be serious and is life-threatening if it develops in someone who is very young or older. The condition is treated with antibiotics and is usually milder if it develops in someone who is older or in a child who is under the age of one. However, it can get worse and more serious in a child or an adult. Bronchiolitis is rare in children under the age of two, but the symptoms can be similar to other illnesses, such as pneumonia, so it's best to consult your doctor immediately if you notice your child is unwell. Source: NHS Choices\nWhat are the symptoms of bronchiolitis?\nBronchiolitis causes a swelling of the airways in the lungs, which causes difficulty breathing.\nThe symptoms are similar to those of other illnesses, such as pneumonia, so it's important to seek medical advice if your child has any of the following symptoms:\nCoughing\nWheezing\nShortness of breath\nFever\nTiredness\nThese symptoms will usually clear up by themselves, but you should consult your doctor if your child does not improve within seven days.\nYou should take your child to the doctor if you are worried about any symptoms and it is unclear what is causing them.\nBronchiolitis can cause other complications, so it's important to seek medical advice as soon as possible if your child is unwell.\nThis includes:\nIf the swelling in the airways in the lungs becomes very severe, this can lead to asthma or pneumonia, where the airways narrow and the lungs can no longer deliver enough"

Prompt: 'What are the signs of bronchiolitis in children and when should I seek medical attention?\n' 
Generated text: '\nBronchiolitis is a very common respiratory tract infection in children. The majority of children will recover without treatment in a few days. Most children with the infection will have a cough and a fever.\n\nAs with other infections in children, bronchiolitis is easily contagious. Prompt: 'What is the cause of Creutzfeldt-Jakob disease?\n' 
Generated text: "\nCreutzfeldt-Jakob disease (CJD) is caused by a brain-destroying protein called prion. Prions are abnormal proteins that are not very stable and don't self-assemble into a structured protein. Prions contain two strands of nucleotides that are twisted or folded in a way that is not normally found in nature. These abnormal proteins can infect other proteins, forming new, abnormal proteins that are the cause of CJD."

The best method of prevention is early detection and early treatment.\n\nHow is Creutzfeldt-Jakob disease diagnosed?\n\nThere is no lab test to diagnose CJD. It stops pumping blood around the body and eventually causes the heart to stop beating.\n\nOnce blood flow to the heart has been restored, the heart muscle cells are able to grow back and contract again, and the heart can start pumping blood again.\n\nPeople who have heart attacks are usually treated in hospital by a cardiologist (heart doctor) or a cardiologist and a surgeon. The aim of treatment is to restore blood flow to the heart and to help the heart muscle to grow back and contract again.'

Prompt: 'What is laryngitis?\n' 
Generated text: '\nLaryngitis is an inflammation of the vocal cords. The voicebox is located in the throat, and the soft tissue and surrounding muscles and bones are connected by the vocal cords. When the larynx becomes inflamed, the voice is muffled, hoarse, and strained.\n\nCauses\n\nThe main cause of laryngitis is viral infections. Common viruses that can cause laryngitis include the cold, flu, and adenovirus. In addition, a common cause of laryngitis is allergic reaction. During a severe allergic reaction, the body’s immune system reacts to the allergen and causes inflammation and swelling in the throat. Other possible causes of laryngitis include smoking, bad posture, and use of antibiotics.\n\nSymptoms\n\nThe symptoms of laryngitis usually begin gradually and worsen over a period of weeks or months. The symptoms may include hoarseness, sore throat, and a change in the voice. Swallowing difficulty is also very common, and people may find that they have trouble breathing. The throat may feel irritated or painful to the touch, and inflammation of the vocal cords may produce a crackling sound.\n\nTreatment\n\nLaryngitis can be treated at home, but symptoms may worsen if left untreated. If you experience a sore throat, your doctor may prescribe over-the-counter throat lozenges or antihistamines. You should also use a humidifier at night to help prevent swelling in your throat and reduce the inflammation. Staying hydrated can also help to reduce swelling.\n\nWhile over-the-counter treatments are often sufficient, some cases of laryngitis are more severe and require medical treatment. In these cases, your doctor may prescribe antibiotics to treat a bacterial infection. In severe cases, laryngitis may need to be treated with surgery, though the surgeon may recommend a procedure called a laryngeal shave, where the vocal cords are separated from each other.\n\nPrevention\n\nYou can prevent laryngitis by avoiding smoking and using a humidifier to help reduce swelling in your throat.\n\nRevision Information\n\nThis content is reviewed regularly and is updated when new and relevant evidence is made available. It is a protein that is produced naturally by the human body to fight off viruses and bacteria. It also has shown promise in reducing the progression of multiple sclerosis.\n\nLeflunomide does not cause any significant side effects, but it is only approved for use in combination with interferon-alpha.
